# Analysis of Ground Truth

The GT numerical expression is:
$$f(t, A) = \frac{0.7391 A^2}{0.8913 A^4 + 1} - 0.3009 A \cdot e^{-0.06776 t}$$

This has two distinct components:
1. A rational function of A: $\frac{c \cdot A^2}{d \cdot A^4 + 1}$
2. An exponential decay in t multiplied by A: $-k \cdot A \cdot e^{-\alpha t}$

The key structural features are:
- The rational part has $A^2$ in numerator and $A^4$ in denominator
- The exponential part is $A \cdot e^{-\alpha t}$ (linear in A, exponential in t)

Let me check each candidate for structural compatibility.

## Systematic Analysis

For a candidate to match, it must be able to produce:
1. A term like $\frac{A^2}{A^4 + \text{const}}$ (rational function with $A^2$ numerator, $A^4$ denominator)
2. A term like $A \cdot e^{-\alpha t}$

Let me scan through candidates looking for these features:

### Candidates with exp(c*t) terms (potential match for $A \cdot e^{-\alpha t}$):

Most candidates have $\exp(c \cdot t)$ terms, but the GT requires this to be multiplied by $A$. Let me check which candidates have $A \cdot \exp(c \cdot t)$.

**Candidates 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 20, 22, 34, 35, 43, 48, 49, 50** have terms like $A \cdot c \cdot \exp(c \cdot t) / (\text{something})$.

### Checking for rational function $A^2/(A^4 + \text{const})$:

None of the candidates explicitly have $A^4$ in the denominator. The denominators are typically linear in A (like $A \cdot c + c$). So I need to check if any combination of terms with linear denominators can produce $A^2/(A^4 + 1)$.

A rational function $\frac{A^2}{A^4+1}$ has degree 2 in numerator and degree 4 in denominator. With denominators that are linear in A (degree 1), we cannot construct a degree-4 denominator through addition of fractions with linear denominators. Even combining two fractions with linear denominators gives at most a quadratic denominator.

### Candidates with log terms:
Many candidates use $\log(cA + 1)$. This is a transcendental function and cannot equal a rational function of A. So candidates relying on log to approximate the rational part cannot match.

### Candidates with exp(A*c) terms:
$e^{cA}$ is also transcendental and cannot equal a rational function.

### Candidates with sin terms:
$\sin(cA + c)$ is transcendental and cannot match a rational function.

### Candidates with $A^c$ power terms:
Terms like $A^{c_0} \cdot c_1$ - even with free constants, a single power of A cannot equal $\frac{A^2}{A^4+1}$.

### Candidates with $1/A^{1/4}$ terms:
These are power functions, not rational functions with $A^4$ denominators.

### Key conclusion:
The GT has a rational function $\frac{A^2}{0.8913 A^4 + 1}$ which requires an $A^4$ term in the denominator. **None of the candidates have denominators with $A^4$ or even $A^2$ terms.** The highest power of A in any denominator is $A^1$ (linear). 

No combination of the available basis functions (linear denominators in A, exponentials, logs, powers, trig functions) can produce a rational function with $A^4$ in the denominator.

Additionally, the $A \cdot e^{-\alpha t}$ term requires the exponential in t to be multiplied by A. While some candidates have this structure, they still cannot produce the rational function part.

After careful examination of all 50 candidates, none can structurally match the ground truth expression $\frac{0.7391 A^2}{0.8913 A^4 + 1} - 0.3009 A e^{-0.06776 t}$.

**GT:** `0.7391218893246799*A**2/(0.8913296033617462*A**4 + 1) - 0.3009370469546767*A*exp(-0.06776739623123975*t)`

The GT has two terms:
1. A rational function of A: `A²/(c₄A⁴ + 1)` scaled by a constant
2. An exponential decay in t multiplied by A: `A*exp(-αt)`

Key structural features:
- The A-dependent rational part is `A²/(A⁴ + const)` — this is NOT a simple rational function like `A/(A+c)` or polynomial
- The t-dependent part is `A*exp(-αt)` — pure exponential decay times A

Let me check each candidate for structural compatibility:

**Candidates with `exp(A*c)` terms (exponential in A):** These cannot match `A²/(A⁴+1)` which is a rational function. Candidates 7, 11, 14-19, 21, 24-26, 32, 37-39, 46 — these have `exp(A*c)` which is fundamentally different from a rational function in A. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates with `log(A*c+1)` terms:** log functions cannot reproduce rational functions like `A²/(A⁴+1)`. Candidates 3, 5, 6, 20, 22, 23, 34, 35, 40, 42, 43, 47-50 — [NO MATCH]

**Candidates with `sin(A*c+c)` terms:** sin cannot match rational functions. Candidates 14, 33, 36, 40, 41 — [NO MATCH]

**Candidates with `1/A^(1/4)` terms:** This basis function doesn't appear in GT and can't be zeroed if it's needed to build the rational part. Candidates 7-11, 15, 23, 27-31, 33, 36, 41, 44 — if the `1/A^(1/4)` is an extra term, we can set its coefficient to 0, but then we need the remaining terms to match GT. Let me check if any remaining structure could work.

**Candidates with `t*exp(c*t)`:** This is NOT the same as `A*exp(ct)`. The GT has `A*exp(ct)`, not `t*exp(ct)`. These are linearly independent. Candidates 8-10, 23, 27, 29-33, 40, 41, 44, 45 — [NO MATCH] (unless they also have a pure `exp(ct)` term and the `t*exp(ct)` can be zeroed, but then we still need `A*exp(ct)`).

Candidate 4: Has `A*c3*exp(c4*t)` and `A*c7*exp(c4*t)/(A*c1+c2)` and `c8*exp(c4*t)` — combined exp(ct) terms, plus `t^c6` terms. Can't build `A²/(A⁴+1)`. [NO MATCH]

Candidate 13: `A*c0/(c1*t+c2) + A^c3*c4 + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7*exp(c8*t) + c9/(c1*t+c2)` — has `A/(t+c)` mixing A and t, and `A^c3` power law. Can't match. [NO MATCH]

After systematic analysis, none of the candidates can reproduce the `A²/(A⁴+1)` rational structure. This requires a degree-2 numerator and degree-4 denominator in A, which none of the candidates provide.
